### <span id="page-75-0"></span>**A Simple Polynomial-Round Extractable Commitments**

In what follows, we describe ideas in [\[BS20\]](#page-70-1) that can be used to convert a post-quantum zero-knowledge protocol to an extractable commitment scheme (assuming quantum hardness of LWE). Specifically, we start with the (polynomial-round) zero-knowledge protocol in [\[Wat09\]](#page-74-1) that can be based on any quantum oneway function, and convert it into a (polynomial-round) extractable commitment scheme.

Let Com(α; β) denote a non-interactive perfectly binding, quantum-hiding commitment to classical string α with randomness β. We also let CDS denote a two-party two-message conditional disclosure of secrets protocol, where in the first message, the receiver outputs a statement x, an NP language L, and purportedly commits to an NP witness for this statement. Next, the sender encodes a secret m in such a way that the receiver can recover m if and only if it previously committed to an NP witness for x. The (informal) security property is that the NP witness is hidden from a semi-honest sender, and the sender's secret m is hidden from a malicious receiver whenever x 6∈ L. It is well-known (eg., [\[OPP14,](#page-73-13) [BGI](#page-69-10)<sup>+</sup>17]) that this can be achieved by combining a specific type of two-message OT (called statistically sender-private OT, that can itself be based on quantum hardness of LWE [\[BD18a\]](#page-69-11)) with garbled circuits.

<span id="page-75-1"></span>Given these components, a polynomial-round extractable commitment is described in Figure [7.](#page-75-1)

### **Extractable Commitments**

**Sender's private input**: A message m ∈ {0, 1} p(λ)

- 1. S sends cmt<sup>S</sup> ← Com(m; rS).
- 2. R sends cmt<sup>R</sup> ← Com(0<sup>λ</sup> ; rR).
- 3. S and R interact with each other in a post-quantum ZK protocol for cmt<sup>R</sup> ∈ L where S acts as V and R acts as P using r<sup>R</sup> as the witness where

$$L = \{c : \exists y \text{ such that } c = \mathsf{Com}(0^{\lambda}; y)\}$$

4. If the proof verifies, S and R execute a post-quantum CDS protocol for cmt<sup>R</sup> ∈ L, where S is CDS sender with secret m and R is CDS receiver with witness r<sup>R</sup> where

$$L = \{c : \exists y \text{ such that } c = \mathsf{Com}(1^{\lambda}; y)\}$$

5. Finally, S and R execute post-quantum ZK where S acts as P and R acts as V. S proves that its transcript until the end of Step 4 is consistent, i.e., there is a consistent message and randomness that generates the sender's transcript until Step 4.

Figure 7: Extractable Commitments

At a high level, the commitment is hiding because any cheating receiver that completes Step 3 will, by the soundness of the ZK protocol, have committed to 0 λ in Step 2. By the perfect binding property of the commitment, this means that the statement of the CDS protocol, in Step 4, is false. Therefore, because the indistinguishability-based security of CDS (as discussed above), the committer's message m remains hidden from a QPT receiver.

The commitment is extractable against quantum committers (which also implies binding), because of the following argument: Consider extractor Ext that in Step 2 generates cmt<sup>R</sup> as Com(1<sup>λ</sup> ; rR) instead of committing to 0 λ . Next, Ext runs ZK.Sim to simulate the proof in Step 3. After this point, Ext uses r<sup>R</sup> as witness in Step 4, which enables it to successfully retrieve m from CDS.

{76}------------------------------------------------

### <span id="page-76-0"></span>B An explicit quantum attack against a classically-secure ZK protocol

In this section, we will present the construction of ZK protocol for which the zero knowledge property holds against classical verifiers, however, there exists an explicit attack w.r.t a malicious quantum verifier. This example is inspired by the recent construction of quantum extraction schemes for NP relations[AP20] where the setting is as follows: The sender  $\mathcal S$  and the receiver  $\mathcal R$  hold an NP instance x. Additionally,  $\mathcal S$  holds a witness w for the instance x. The desired property is the following: i) Extractability: For any QPT malicious  $\mathcal S$ , there exists a QPT extractor that can extract a valid witness w' for x, ii) Zero-Knowledge: For any PPT malicious  $\mathcal R$ , there exists a PPT simulator which can simulate the view of  $\mathcal R$  without having access to w.

The extraction scheme presented in [AP20] makes use of the "test of quantumness" protocol [BCM<sup>+</sup>18] as a key ingredient which, as the name suggests, is used to attest whether the prover is a quantum machine or a classical one. The authors leverage this test to construct a quantum extraction protocol (i.e it admits a quantum extractor) secure against classical receivers which is referred to as to as cQEXT. We note that the quantum extractor construction presented in [AP20] is straight-line i.e. it does not perform any kind of quantum rewinding [Wat09, Unr12] on  $\mathcal{S}$ . Also, the extractor makes only black-box use of the malicious  $\mathcal{S}$  i.e. it does not make any use of the circuit representation of a malicious  $\mathcal{S}$ . As we will see shortly, these two properties will be crucial in the construction of our counterexample. Our counterexample involves a classical prover  $\mathcal{P}(x,w)$  interacting with a classical verifier  $\mathcal{V}(x)$  in the following manner:

- 1.  $\mathcal{P}$  and  $\mathcal{V}$  engage in a cQEXT protocol where  $\mathcal{P}$  acts a cQEXT sender using (x, w) and  $\mathcal{V}$  acts as a cQEXT receiver using x.
- 2.  $\mathcal{P}(x, w)$  and  $\mathcal{V}(x)$  engage in a standard classical zero knowledge proof protocol which is post-quantum secure.
- 3.  $\mathcal V$  outputs 1 if the proof in Step 2 is accepting. Otherwise, it outputs 0.

The soundness of the above protocol follows from the soundness of the ZK protocol in Step 2. Also, zero-knowledge property of the above protocol w.r.t classical verifiers follows from the zero-knowledge property of the cQEXT protocol in Step 1 and ZK protocol in Step 2. However, the protocol is not zero-knowledge against a malicious QPT verifier  $\mathcal{V}^*$  for the following simple reason:  $\mathcal{V}^*$  can simply execute the extractor algorithm for the cQEXT protocol in Step 1 and therefore retrieve the witness w completely. The reason it will be able to do so without any issue is because the cQEXT extractor is black-box and straight-line. Hence, a malicious QPT verifier, which does not have any rewinding ability or access to the code of prover, can still execute the extractor algorithm seamlessly.

### <span id="page-76-1"></span>C Tag Amplification: Remaining Analysis

Here, we prove Lemma 7.2.

Let  $tag \in [2^{t/2}]$  denote the tag used by the committer in the left session and  $tag' \in [2^{t/2}]$  be the tag used by the MIM in the right session. Observe that, two sets of decomposed tags  $\{tag_i\}_{i\in[t/2]}$  and  $\{tag_i'\}_{i\in[t/2]}$ , derived from two distinct tags, tag and tag', are such that  $\exists \alpha \in [t/2]$  s.t.  $\forall i \in [t/2] : tag'_{\alpha} \neq tag_i$ 

For any values u (respectively v) committed to by C in the left session, denote by u' (respectively v') the value committed to by the MIM in the right session. Additionally, let  $u_i$  (resp,  $v_i$ ) denote the value committed to by C in the  $i^{th}$  parallel execution of nmCom as part of the left commitment and let  $u_i'$  (resp,  $v_i'$ ) denote the value committed to by MIM in the  $i^{th}$  parallel execution of nmCom as part of the right commitment. The soundness of ZK ensures that when the proof verifies:

<span id="page-76-2"></span>
$$\Pr[u' \neq u'_{\alpha}] = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \text{ and } \Pr[v' \neq v'_{\alpha}] = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$$
 (17)

where the probability is over the randomness of honest verifier, and  $\alpha$  denotes the first index in the real (resp., simulated) experiments such that for every  $i \in [t/2]$ ,  $tag'_{\alpha} \neq tag_{i}$ . Whenever the proof does not

{77}------------------------------------------------

verify, the commitment is not 'valid' and u' (resp. v') =  $\bot$ .

Next, recall that in the real world,  $VIEW_{MIM_{\lambda}}\langle C(u), MIM(\rho_{\lambda}), R\rangle(1^{\lambda}, tag, tag')$  denotes the joint distribution of the view of MIM along with the value u' committed to in the right session when the left committer obtains input u. Similarly,  $VIEW_{MIM_{\lambda}}\langle C(v), MIM(\rho_{\lambda}), R\rangle(1^{\lambda}, tag, tag')$  denotes the joint distribution of the view of MIM along with the value v' committed to in the right session when the right committer obtains input v.

By Equation (17), whenever the MIM's proof verifies, v' can be replaced by  $v'_{\alpha}$  in the distribution VIEW<sub>MIM $_{\lambda}</sub> <math>\langle \mathsf{C}(v), \mathsf{MIM}(\rho_{\lambda}), \mathsf{R} \rangle (1^{\lambda}, \mathsf{tag}, \mathsf{tag}')$ . Similarly, u' can be replaced by  $u'_{\alpha}$  in the distribution VIEW<sub>MIM $_{\lambda}</sub> <math>\langle \mathsf{C}(u), \mathsf{MIM}(\rho_{\lambda}), \mathsf{R} \rangle (1^{\lambda}, \mathsf{tag}, \mathsf{tag}')$  to yield a statistically indistinguishable distribution VIEW<sub>MIM $_{\lambda}</sub> <math>\langle \mathsf{C}(u), \mathsf{MIM}(\rho_{\lambda}), \mathsf{R} \rangle (1^{\lambda}, \mathsf{tag}, \mathsf{tag}')$ .</sub></sub></sub>

It suffices to prove that:

$$\{\mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}_{\lambda}}'\langle\mathsf{C}(u),\mathsf{MIM}(\rho_{\lambda}),\mathsf{R}\rangle(1^{\lambda},\mathsf{tag},\mathsf{tag}')\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_{c}\mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}_{\lambda}}'\langle\mathsf{C}(v),\mathsf{MIM}(\rho_{\lambda}),\mathsf{R}\rangle(1^{\lambda},\mathsf{tag},\mathsf{tag}') \tag{18}$$

To that end, we define the following collections of random variables (each indexed by  $\lambda$ ). Each is defined with respect to the adversary MIM =  $\{MIM_{\lambda}, \rho_{\lambda}\}_{{\lambda} \in \mathbb{N}}$  that we consider. Throughout, when we say abort, we mean that MIM\* aborts before Step 2, or that the MIM fails to provide an accepting proof.

- Let  $\Pr_{\mathsf{u}}^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM})$  be the probability that MIM aborts in  $\mathsf{VIEW}'_{\mathsf{MIM}_{\lambda}}\langle\mathsf{C}(u),\mathsf{MIM}(\rho_{\lambda}),\mathsf{R}\rangle(1^{\lambda},\mathsf{tag},\mathsf{tag}')$ .
- Let  $\mathsf{Pr}^{\mathsf{Abort}}_{\mathsf{v}}(\mathsf{MIM})$  be the probability that MIM aborts in  $\mathsf{VIEW}'_{\mathsf{MIM}_{\lambda}}\langle\mathsf{C}(v),\mathsf{MIM}(\rho_{\lambda}),\mathsf{R}\rangle(1^{\lambda},\mathsf{tag},\mathsf{tag}')$ .
- Let  $VIEW_u(MIM) := \{VIEW'_{MIM_{\lambda}} \langle C(u), MIM(\rho_{\lambda}), R \rangle (1^{\lambda}, tag, tag')\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$
- Let  $VIEW_v(MIM) := \{VIEW'_{MIM_\lambda}\langle C(v), MIM(\rho_\lambda), R\rangle(1^\lambda, \mathsf{tag}, \mathsf{tag}')\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$
- $\bullet$  Let  $\mathsf{VIEW}^\mathsf{No\ Abort}_u(\mathsf{MIM})$  be the distribution  $\mathsf{VIEW}_u(\mathsf{MIM})$  conditioned on there not being an abort.
- $\bullet$  Let  $\mathsf{VIEW}^{\mathsf{Abort}}_u(\mathsf{MIM})$  be the distribution  $\mathsf{VIEW}_u(\mathsf{MIM})$  conditioned on there being an abort.
- $\bullet$  Let  $\mathsf{VIEW}^\mathsf{No\ Abort}_v(\mathsf{MIM})$  be the distribution  $\mathsf{VIEW}_v(\mathsf{MIM})$  conditioned on there not being an abort.
- $\bullet$  Let  $\mathsf{VIEW}^{\mathsf{Abort}}_v(\mathsf{MIM})$  be the distribution  $\mathsf{VIEW}_v(\mathsf{MIM})$  conditioned on there being an abort.

The following distributions will not be used explicitly in the hybrids, but will be convenient to define for the proof.

- Let  $VIEW_{v,\perp}(MIM)$  be the distribution  $VIEW_v(MIM)$ , except that whenever an abort occurs, the distribution outputs  $\perp$ .
- Let  $VIEW_{v,\perp}^{Abort}(MIM)$  be the distribution  $VIEW_v(MIM)$ , except that if an abort *does not* occur, the distribution outputs  $\perp$ .
- Let  $VIEW_{u,\perp}(MIM)$  be the distribution  $VIEW_u(MIM)$ , except that whenever an abort occurs, the distribution outputs  $\perp$ .
- Let  $VIEW_{u,\perp}^{Abort}(MIM)$  be the distribution  $VIEW_u(MIM)$ , except that if an abort *does not* occur, the distribution outputs  $\perp$ .

{78}------------------------------------------------

We show that  $VIEW_u(MIM) \approx_c VIEW_v(MIM)$  via a sequence on hybrids. In particular, we prove:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{VIEW}_v(\mathsf{MIM}) &\overset{(1)}{\equiv} (1 - \mathsf{Pr}_v^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM})) \mathsf{VIEW}_v^{\mathsf{No} \ \mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM}) + (\mathsf{Pr}_v^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM})) \mathsf{VIEW}_v^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM}) \\ &\overset{(2)}{\approx}_s (1 - \mathsf{Pr}_u^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM})) \mathsf{VIEW}_v^{\mathsf{No} \ \mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM}) + (\mathsf{Pr}_u^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM})) \mathsf{VIEW}_v^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM}) \\ &\overset{(3)}{\approx}_c (1 - \mathsf{Pr}_u^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM})) \mathsf{VIEW}_u^{\mathsf{No} \ \mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM}) + (\mathsf{Pr}_u^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM})) \mathsf{VIEW}_v^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM}) \\ &\overset{(4)}{\approx}_c (1 - \mathsf{Pr}_u^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM})) \mathsf{VIEW}_u^{\mathsf{No} \ \mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM}) + (\mathsf{Pr}_u^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM})) \mathsf{VIEW}_u^{\mathsf{Abort}}(\mathsf{MIM}) \\ &\overset{(5)}{\equiv} \mathsf{VIEW}_u(\mathsf{MIM}), \end{split}$$

#### where

- 1. The equalities (1) and (5) follow by definition.
- 2. The indistinguishability (2) follows as a corollary of Claim C.1. Indeed,  $VIEW_{u,\perp}(MIM) \approx_c VIEW_{v,\perp}(MIM)$  in particular implies that the difference in the probability that the MIM aborts in the real interaction versus the simulated interaction is negligible.
- 3. The indistinguishability (3) follows as a corollary of Claim C.1. This can be seen by considering two cases. First, if the probability that the MIM aborts in the real interaction is negligible, then  $\mathsf{VIEW}_v^\mathsf{No\ Abort}(\mathsf{MIM}) \approx_c \mathsf{VIEW}_u^\mathsf{No\ Abort}(\mathsf{MIM})$  directly follows from Claim C.1, and the indistinguishability follows. Otherwise, this probability is non-negligible, meaning that  $\mathsf{VIEW}_v^\mathsf{Abort}(\mathsf{MIM})$  is efficiently sampleable. Thus, a reduction to Claim C.1 can sample from the distribution  $\mathsf{VIEW}_v^\mathsf{Abort}(\mathsf{MIM})$  whenever it receives  $\bot$  from its challenger.<sup>21</sup>
- 4. The indistinguishability (4) follows as a corollary of Claim C.3 via a similar analysis as the last step.

#### <span id="page-78-0"></span>Claim C.1.

$$\mathsf{VIEW}_{u,\perp}(\mathsf{MIM}) \approx_c \mathsf{VIEW}_{v,\perp}(\mathsf{MIM})$$

*Proof.* We prove this via a sequence of hybrids. We use  $\mathcal{H}_k$  to denote the joint distribution of MIM's view (consisting of commitment and proof transcripts along with MIM's state) and the value that MIM commits to in the right session of Hybrid k, using tag  $\operatorname{tag}'_{\alpha}$ , where  $\alpha$  denotes the smallest index such that  $\operatorname{tag}'_{\alpha} \neq \operatorname{tag}_i$  for every  $i \in [t/2]$ .

 $\mathcal{H}_1$ : In this hybrid, the challenger executes the simulator ZK.Sim $(1^{\lambda}, x_{\lambda}, V_{\lambda}^*, \sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})})$  on  $V_{\lambda}^*$ , which denotes a wrapper around the portion of the MIM that participates in Stage 2 of the protocol, and an instance-advice distribution  $(x_{\lambda}, \sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})})$  defined as follows:

- Set the state of  $MIM_{\lambda}$  to be  $\rho_{\lambda}$ .
- Execute Stages 0 and 1 of the protocol the same way as in the experiment  $VIEW_{u,\perp}(MIM)$ , and set  $x, w, \mathcal{L}$  according to Protocol 5 on behalf of  $\mathcal{C}$ .
- Let  $\sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})}$  denote the joint distribution of the protocol transcript, the state of the MIM at the end of Stage 1, and the value  $v'_{\alpha}$  committed by the MIM with tag  $tag'_{\alpha}$ .

If there is an abort during sampling, or ZK.Sim causes  $V_{\lambda}^*$  to abort (this includes the MIM failing to provide an accepting proof), then output  $\bot$ . By Claim 6.2,

$$\mathsf{VIEW}_{u,\perp}(\mathsf{MIM}) \approx_c \mathcal{H}_1$$

<span id="page-78-1"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>21</sup>A more formal analysis of this can be found in [BS20, Lemma 3.2].

{79}------------------------------------------------

 $\mathcal{H}_2$ : In this hybrid, the challenger behaves identically to  $\mathcal{H}_1$ , except when generating  $(x_\lambda, \sigma_\lambda^{(x_\lambda)})$ , it replaces the commitment to u with a commitment to v in the first parallel repetition, with  $tag_1$ , of nmCom (while executing all other parallel repetitions the same way as  $\mathcal{H}_1$ ). If there is an abort during sampling, or ZK.Sim causes  $V_\lambda^*$  to abort, then output  $\bot$ .

We prove in Claim C.2 that by one-to-one non-malleability of nmCom, for every  $u, v \in \{0, 1\}^{p(\lambda)}$ ,

$$\mathcal{H}_1 \approx_c \mathcal{H}_2$$

 $\mathcal{H}_i$  for  $i \in [3, (t/2+1)]$ : In this hybrid, the challenger behaves identically to  $\mathcal{H}_{i-1}$ , except when generating  $(x_{\lambda}, \sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})})$ , it replaces the commitment to u with a commitment to v in the  $(i-1)^{th}$  parallel repetition, with tag tag<sub>i-1</sub>, of nmCom (while executing all other parallel repetitions the same way as  $\mathcal{H}_{i-1}$ ). If there is an abort during sampling, or ZK.Sim causes V\* to abort, then output  $\bot$ .

We prove in Claim C.2 that by one-to-one non-malleability of nmCom, for every  $u,v\in\{0,1\}^{p(\lambda)}$  and every  $i\in[3,t/2+1]$ ,

$$\mathcal{H}_{i-1} \approx_c \mathcal{H}_i$$

Finally, by claim 6.2, we have that

$$\mathcal{H}_{(t/2+1)} \approx_c \mathsf{VIEW}_{u,\perp}(\mathsf{MIM})$$

Next, we state and prove Claim C.2.

<span id="page-79-0"></span>**Claim C.2.** For all  $u, v \in \{0, 1\}^{p(\lambda)}$  and all  $i \in [2, t/2 + 1]$ ,

$$\mathcal{H}_i \approx_c \mathcal{H}_{i-1}$$
 (19)

*Proof.* Suppose Claim C.2 is false. Then there exists values (u, v), some  $i \in [2, t/2 + 1]$  and a polynomial  $poly(\cdot)$  such that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,

$$|\Pr[\mathsf{MIM}(\mathcal{H}_i) = 1] - \Pr[\mathsf{MIM}(\mathcal{H}_{i-1}) = 1]| \ge \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)}$$
 (20)

We will demonstrate an adversary  $MIM^{\beta}$  that contradicts the non-malleability of nmCom according to Definition 7.1, i.e. we will show that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,

$$\begin{split} & \left| \Pr[\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta} \big( \mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}_{\lambda}} \langle \mathsf{C}(v), \mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}(\rho_{\lambda}), \mathsf{R} \rangle (1^{\lambda}, \mathsf{tag}_{i-1}, \mathsf{tag}_{\alpha}') \big) = 1 \right] \\ & - \Pr[\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta} \big( \mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}_{\lambda}} \langle \mathsf{C}(u), \mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}(\rho_{\lambda}), \mathsf{R} \rangle (1^{\lambda}, \mathsf{tag}_{i-1}, \mathsf{tag}_{\alpha}') \big) = 1 \right] \Big| \geq \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} \end{split} \tag{21}$$

where the two distributions  $\mathsf{MIM}^\beta \big( \mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}^\beta_\lambda} \langle \mathsf{C}(v), \mathsf{MIM}^\beta(\rho_\lambda), \mathsf{R} \rangle (1^\lambda, \mathsf{tag}_{i-1}, \mathsf{tag}'_\alpha) \big) = 1$  and  $\mathsf{MIM}^\beta \big( \mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}^\beta_\lambda} \langle \mathsf{C}(u), \mathsf{MIM}^\beta(\rho_\lambda), \mathsf{R} \rangle (1^\lambda, \mathsf{tag}_{i-1}, \mathsf{tag}'_\alpha) \big) = 1$  correspond to honest commitments to v and u respectively, for the small-tag commitment scheme.

 $\mathsf{MIM}^\beta$  is defined as follows:

- 1. Obtain input values v, u, and begin an interaction with a challenger for nmCom.
- 2. Emulate the role of honest committer and honest receiver in an interaction with MIM executing Protocol 5. In more detail, in the role of a committer in a left session, participate in a session of Protocol 5 with MIM as receiver. At the same time, play the role of the receiver in a right session with MIM as committer. Recall that Protocol 5 contains k repetitions of nmCom and ZK.
- 3. In the left session, embed the challenger's messages in the  $(i-1)^{th}$  instance of nmCom, and forward the response of MIM corresponding to the  $(i-1)^{th}$  instance to the challenger. Execute remaining instances according to the strategy in  $\mathcal{H}_{i-1}$ .

{80}------------------------------------------------

- 4. In the right session, forward the message obtained from MIM in the  $\alpha^{th}$  instance of nmCom to the challenger, and embed the challenger's response for that round as receiver message in the  $\alpha^{th}$  instance. Use honest receiver strategy for all other instances of nmCom in the right session.
- 5. Obtain value  $v'_{\alpha}$  from the challenger of the non-malleable commitment (representing the value in the commitment sent by  $\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}$  to the challenger on the right).
- 6. Use the transcript, the obtained value  $v'_{\alpha}$  and the state of MIM to define the instance-advice sample, and then execute  $\mathsf{ZK}.\mathsf{Sim}(1^{\lambda}, x_{\lambda}, \mathsf{V}^*_{\lambda}, \sigma^{(x_{\lambda})}_{\lambda})$ .
- 7. If an abort occurs at any point, output  $\perp$ .

We now analyze the probability that  $MIM^{\beta}$  successfully contradicts Definition 7.1. To this end, we note that:

$$\Pr[\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}\big(\mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}_{\lambda}}\langle\mathsf{C}(u),\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}(\rho_{\lambda}),\mathsf{R}\rangle(1^{\lambda},\mathsf{tag}_{i-1},\mathsf{tag}_{\alpha}')\big)=1]=\Pr[\mathsf{MIM}(\mathcal{H}_{i-1})=1] \tag{22}$$

$$\Pr[\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}\big(\mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}_{\lambda}}\langle\mathsf{C}(v),\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}(\rho_{\lambda}),\mathsf{R}\rangle(1^{\lambda},\mathsf{tag}_{i-1},\mathsf{tag}_{\alpha}')\big)=1]=\Pr[\mathsf{MIM}(\mathcal{H}_{i})=1] \tag{23}$$

Therefore, for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,

$$\begin{split} \Big| \Pr[\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta} \big( \mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}_{\lambda}} \langle \mathsf{C}(u), \mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}(\rho_{\lambda}), \mathsf{R} \rangle (1^{\lambda}, \mathsf{tag}_{i-1}, \mathsf{tag}_{\alpha}') \big) = 1] \\ - \Pr[\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta} \big( \mathsf{VIEW}_{\mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}_{\lambda}} \langle \mathsf{C}(v), \mathsf{MIM}^{\beta}(\rho_{\lambda}), \mathsf{R} \rangle (1^{\lambda}, \mathsf{tag}_{i-1}, \mathsf{tag}_{\alpha}') \big) = 1] \Big| = \\ \Big| \Pr[\mathsf{MIM}(\boldsymbol{\mathcal{H}}_{i-1}) = 1] - \Pr[\mathsf{MIM}(\boldsymbol{\mathcal{H}}_{i}) = 1] \Big| \geq \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} \end{split}$$

which is a contradiction, as desired.

This completes the proof of Claim C.1.  $\Box$ 

#### <span id="page-80-0"></span>Claim C.3.

$$\mathsf{VIEW}^{\mathsf{Abort}}_{u,\perp}(\mathsf{MIM}) \approx_{c} \mathsf{VIEW}^{\mathsf{Abort}}_{v,\perp}(\mathsf{MIM})$$

*Proof.* We prove this via a sequence of hybrids. We use  $\mathcal{H}_k$  to denote the joint distribution of the MIM's view (consisting of commitment and proof transcripts along with the MIM's state) in Hybrid k.

 $\mathcal{H}_1$ : In this hybrid, the challenger executes one iteration of the simulator ZK.SimAbort $_{\perp}(1^{\lambda}, x_{\lambda}, \mathsf{V}_{\lambda}^*, \sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})})$  on  $\mathsf{V}_{\lambda}^*$ , where  $\mathsf{V}_{\lambda}^*$  denotes the portion of the MIM that participates in Stage 2 of the protocol, and an instance-advice distribution  $(x_{\lambda}, \sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})})$  defined as follows:

- Set the state of  $MIM_{\lambda}$  to be  $\rho_{\lambda}$ .
- Execute Stage 1 of the protocol the same way as in the experiment real(MIM), and set  $x, w, \mathcal{L}$  according to Protocol 5 on behalf of  $\mathcal{C}$ .
- If an abort occurs, output the transcript and state of the MIM until the abort.
- Otherwise, let  $\sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})}$  denote the joint distribution of the protocol transcript and the state of the MIM at the end of Stage 1.

If  $\mathsf{ZK}.\mathsf{SimAbort}_{\perp}(1^{\lambda}, x_{\lambda}, \mathsf{V}_{\lambda}^{*}, \sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})})$  outputs a non-aborting transcript and state, output  $\perp$ , otherwise return the output of  $\mathsf{ZK}.\mathsf{SimAbort}_{\perp}(1^{\lambda}, x_{\lambda}, \mathsf{V}_{\lambda}^{*}, \sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})})$ . By Claim 6.3,

$$\mathsf{VIEW}^{\mathsf{Abort}}_{u,\perp}(\mathsf{MIM}) \approx_c \, \mathcal{H}_1$$

{81}------------------------------------------------

 $\mathcal{H}_2$ : In this hybrid, the challenger behaves identically to  $\mathcal{H}_1$ , except when generating  $(x_\lambda, \sigma_\lambda^{(x_\lambda)})$ , it replaces the commitment to u with a commitment to v in the first parallel repetition, with  $tag_1$ , of nmCom (while executing all other parallel repetitions the same way as  $\mathcal{H}_1$ ). If a non-aborting transcript is produced, then output  $\bot$ .

We prove in Claim C.4 that by hiding of nmCom, for every  $u, v \in \{0, 1\}^{p(\lambda)}$ ,

$$\mathcal{H}_1 \approx_c \mathcal{H}_2$$

 $\mathcal{H}_i$  for  $i \in [3, (t/2+1)]$ : In this hybrid, the challenger behaves identically to  $\mathcal{H}_{i-1}$ , except when generating  $(x_{\lambda}, \sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})})$ , it replaces the commitment to u with a commitment to v in the  $(i-1)^{th}$  parallel repetition, with tag  $tag_{i-1}$ , of nmCom (while executing all other parallel repetitions the same way as  $\mathcal{H}_{i-1}$ ). If a non-aborting transcript is produced, then output  $\bot$ . We prove in Claim C.4 that by hiding of nmCom, for every  $u, v \in \{0,1\}^{p(\lambda)}$  and every  $i \in [3, t/2+1]$ ,

$$\mathcal{H}_{i-1} \approx_c \mathcal{H}_i$$

Finally, by claim 6.3, we have that

$$\mathcal{H}_{(t/2+1)} \approx_c \mathsf{VIEW}_{v,\perp}(\mathsf{MIM})$$

Next, we state and prove Claim C.4.

<span id="page-81-0"></span>**Claim C.4.** For every  $u, v \in \{0, 1\}^{p(\lambda)}$  and all  $i \in [2, t/2 + 1]$ ,

$$\mathcal{H}_i \approx_c \mathcal{H}_{i-1}$$

*Proof.* Suppose Claim C.4 is false. Then there exist  $u, v \in \{0, 1\}^{p(\lambda)}$ , some  $i \in [2, t/2 + 1]$ , a PPT distinguisher D and a polynomial  $poly(\cdot)$  such that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,

$$|\Pr[D(\mathcal{H}_i) = 1] - \Pr[D(\mathcal{H}_{i-1}) = 1]| \ge \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)}$$
 (24)

We will demonstrate a receiver that contradicts the hiding property of nmCom, i.e. we will show that there exists R\* such that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,

$$|\Pr[\mathsf{R}^*(\mathsf{nmCom}\langle\mathsf{C}(u),\mathsf{R}^*\rangle) = 1] - \Pr[\mathsf{R}^*(\mathsf{nmCom}\langle\mathsf{C}(v),\mathsf{R}^*\rangle) = 1]| \ge \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} \tag{25}$$

R\* obtains input u, v, and begins an interaction with a challenger for the hiding of nmCom. It then emulates the role of honest committer and honest receiver in an interaction with MIM, executing Protocol 5. In the left session, it embeds the challenger's messages in the  $(i-1)^{th}$  instance of nmCom, and forwards the response of MIM corresponding to the  $(i-1)^{th}$  instance to the challenger. It executes the remaining instances in the left session, and all instances of the right session according to the strategy in  $\mathcal{H}_{i-1}$ . Next, it uses the transcript and state of the MIM to define the instance-advice sample, and executes one iteration of ZK.SimAbort $_{\perp}(1^{\lambda}, x_{\lambda}, \mathsf{V}_{\lambda}^{*}, \sigma_{\lambda}^{(x_{\lambda})})$ .

If an abort occurs at some point, then  $R^*$  runs  $D(\tau, st)$  where  $\tau$  and st denote the transcript and the state of the adversary until the point in the protocol where the abort occurs. If no abort occurs throughout the protocol, then  $R^*$  outputs 0.

We now analyze the probability that R\* successfully contradicts Definition 7.1. Here, we note that:

$$\Pr[\mathsf{R}^*(\mathsf{nmCom}\langle\mathsf{C}(u),\mathsf{R}^*\rangle)=1] = \Pr[D(\mathcal{H}_{i-1})=1] \text{ and,}$$
$$\Pr[\mathsf{R}^*(\mathsf{nmCom}\langle\mathsf{C}(v),\mathsf{R}^*\rangle)=1] = \Pr[D(\mathcal{H}_i)=1]$$

Therefore, for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,

$$\begin{split} & \left| \Pr[\mathsf{R}^*(\mathsf{nmCom}\langle \mathsf{C}(u), \mathsf{R}^*\rangle) = 1] - \Pr[\mathsf{R}^*(\mathsf{nmCom}\langle \mathsf{C}(v), \mathsf{R}^*\rangle) = 1] \right| \\ & = \left| \Pr[D(\mathcal{H}_{i-1}) = 1] - \Pr[D(\mathcal{H}_i) = 1] \right| \geq \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} \end{split}$$

which is a contradiction, as desired. This completes the proof of Claim C.4.

{82}------------------------------------------------

Together, these claims complete the proof of Lemma 7.2.

# <span id="page-82-0"></span>D Multi-Committer Extractable Commitments against Arbitrary Distinguishers

Recall that in the setting of multi-committer extractable commitments 5.1, we only considered computational indistinguishability against any *compliant* non-uniform polynomial-size quantum distinguisher D. We will now demonstrate how to upgrade any multi-committer extractable commitment secure against any compliant non-uniform polynomial-size quantum distinguisher to one which is secure against any *arbitrary* non-uniform polynomial-size quantum distinguisher. The resulting commitment admits an extractor that makes use of the Quantum Rewinding lemma 3.1 to successfully generate both explainable and non-explainable transcripts.

**Construction.** Let eCom denote any multi committer extractable commitment protocol which admits an extractor Ext. Consider a modified version of the protocol eCom' which is identical to eCom except that at the very end, each of the committers  $\{C_i\}_{i\in[n]}$  sends a constant-round ZK argument to the receiver attesting to the fact that the committer messages were explainable. If the verification check passes for all the arguments, the receiver accepts all the commitments. Otherwise it rejects all the commitments, and the committed value is set to  $\bot$ . We denote this by Reject.

**Analysis.** Assuming eCom admits an extractor Ext which satisfies the extractability property against compliant distinguishers, we will construct an extractor Ext' for eCom' which satisifies the extractability property against arbitrary distinguishers. The extractor Ext' consists of a randomized extractor Ext<sub>comb</sub> will consist of two sub-extractors, namely  $\text{Ext}_r$  and  $\text{Ext}_{nr}$ . The purpose of  $\text{Ext}_r$  is to simulate a transcript which generates a Reject whereas the purpose of  $\text{Ext}_{nr}$  is to simulate a transcript which does not generate a Reject.

At a high level,  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}}$  will randomly call one of the two sub-extractors and try to produce a transcript which is indistinguishable from the real view. Looking ahead, this will result in the  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}}$  outputting a quantum state OUT that is indistinguishable from the real verifier output conditioned on  $\mathsf{OUT} \neq \mathsf{Fail}$ . Furthermore,  $\mathsf{OUT} \neq \mathsf{Fail}$  will occur with probability negligibly close to 1/2 (due to random choice of executing either  $\mathsf{Ext}_r$  or  $\mathsf{Ext}_{nr}$  and the computational indistinguishability of the view generated by  $\mathsf{Ext}_r$  and  $\mathsf{Ext}_{nr}$ ). In other words,  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}}$  is going to succeed in extraction only with probability (negligibly close to) 1/2. Once we have this, we can apply Watrous' quantum rewinding lemma 3.1 to amplify the success probability from  $\approx 1/2$  to  $\approx 1$ .

We will now show the construction of  $Ext_{nr}$ ,  $Ext_r$ ,  $Ext_{comb}$  and finally Ext'.

$$\operatorname{Ext}_{nr}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{n}, I, \mathsf{C}_{\lambda}^{*}, \rho)$$
:

- 1. Execute the extractor  $\operatorname{Ext}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{n}, I, C_{\lambda}^{*}, \rho_{\lambda})$  on the adversary  $\mathsf{C}_{\lambda}^{*}$  (which controls a subset I of committers).
- 2. Participate as a honest verifier in |I| ZK argument sessions with  $C_{\lambda}^*$  where  $C_{\lambda}^*$  sends messages on behalf of the prover.
- 3. Execute the verification algorithm on all |I| argument transcripts. If verification check passes for all |I| arguments, then accept all the commitments. Otherwise, say Reject occurs.
- 4. If Reject occurs, discard all information saved so far and output Fail. Otherwise output  $C_{\lambda}^{*}$ 's inner state and the extracted value.

{83}------------------------------------------------

$$\operatorname{Ext}_r(1^{\lambda}, 1^n, I, \mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}, \rho)$$
:

- 1. Interact with  $C_{\lambda}^*$  as an honest receiver of eCom'. If the verification check fails for some ZK argument transcript, count it as a Reject.
- 2. If Reject does not occur, discard all information saved so far and output Fail. Otherwise output  $C_{\lambda}^{*}$ 's inner state, the transcript and  $\bot$  as the extracted value.

$$\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{n}, I, \mathsf{C}_{\lambda}^{*}, \rho)$$
: Sample  $b \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \{r, nr\}$  and execute  $\mathsf{Ext}_{b}$ .

$$\operatorname{Ext}'(1^{\lambda}, 1^{n}, I, \mathsf{C}_{\lambda}^{*}, \rho)$$
:

- 1. Generate the circuit  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb},\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda}$  which is the circuit implementation of  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}}$  with hardwired input  $\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda$ , that is, the only input to  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb},\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda}$  is the quantum state  $\rho$ .
- 2. Let R be the algorithm from Lemma 3.1. The output of the extractor is  $R(\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}},\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda,\rho,\lambda)$

The following claim is similar to the definition of multi-committer extractability stated in Section 5.1 but generalized to handle *arbitrary* distinguishers (instead of just compliant ones).

**Claim D.1.** For any arbitrary non-uniform polynomial-size quantum distinguisher  $\mathsf{D}' = \{\mathsf{D}'_{\lambda}, \sigma_{\lambda}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ , there exists a negligible function  $\mu(\cdot)$ , such that for all adversaries  $\mathsf{C}^* = \{\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}, \rho_{\lambda}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  representing a subset of n committers, namely,  $\{\mathsf{C}_i\}_{i \in I}$  for some set  $I \subseteq [n]$ , the following holds for all polynomial-size sequences of inputs  $\{\{m_{i,\lambda}\}_{i \notin I}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ .

$$\begin{aligned} & \left| \Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}'(\mathsf{VIEW'}_{\mathsf{C}_{\lambda}^*}^{\mathsf{msg}}(\langle \mathsf{R}, \mathsf{C}_{\lambda}^*(\rho_{\lambda}), \{\mathsf{C}_{i}(m_{i,\lambda})\}_{i \notin I} \rangle (1^{\lambda}, 1^{n})), \sigma_{\lambda}) = 1] \right. \\ & \left. - \Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}'(\mathsf{Ext}'(1^{\lambda}, 1^{n}, I, \mathsf{C}_{\lambda}^*, \rho_{\lambda}), \sigma_{\lambda}) = 1] \right| \leq \mu(\lambda). \end{aligned}$$

Here VIEW' $_{\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}}^{\mathsf{msg}}(\langle \mathsf{R}, \mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}(\rho_{\lambda}), \{\mathsf{C}_i(m_i)\}_{i \notin I}\rangle(1^{\lambda}, 1^n))$  is defined to consist of the following:

- The view of  $C_{\lambda}^*$  on eCom' interaction with the honest receiver R and set  $\{C_i(m_i)\}_{i\notin I}$  of honest parties; this view includes a set of transcripts  $\{\tau_i\}_{i\in I}$  and a state st.
- A set of strings  $\{m_i\}_{i\in I}$ , where each  $m_i$  is defined relative to  $\tau_i$  as follows. If there exists  $m_i', r_i$  such that  $\mathsf{R}(1^\lambda, \tau_i, m_i', r_i) = 1$ , then  $m_i = m_i'$ , otherwise,  $m_i = \bot$ .

We will prove the above claim in several steps:

- 1. Simulating non Reject interactions using  $Ext_{nr}$
- 2. Simulating Reject interations using  $Ext_r$
- 3. Applying Watrous rewinding lemma on the combined extractor Ext<sub>comb</sub>

First, we introduce some notation:

- Let  $\operatorname{Ext}_{r,\perp}$  be the same distribution as  $\operatorname{Ext}_r(1^\lambda,1^n,I,\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda,\rho_\lambda)$  except that whenever a Reject does not occur, the distribution output is  $\perp$
- Let  $\operatorname{Ext}_{nr,\perp}$  be the same distribution as  $\operatorname{Ext}_{nr}(1^{\lambda},1^{n},I,\mathsf{C}_{\lambda}^{*},\rho_{\lambda})$  except that whenever a Reject occurs, the distribution output is  $\perp$
- Let  $\mathsf{VIEW}'_{r,\perp}$  be the same distribution as  $\mathsf{VIEW}'^{\mathsf{msg}}_{\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}}(\langle \mathsf{R},\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}(\rho_{\lambda}),\{\mathsf{C}_i(m_{i,\lambda})\}_{i\notin I}\rangle(1^{\lambda},1^n))$  except that whenever a Reject does not occur, the distribution output is  $\bot$
- Let  $\mathsf{VIEW}'_{nr,\perp}$  be the same distribution as  $\mathsf{VIEW}'^{\mathsf{rmsg}}_{\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}}(\langle \mathsf{R},\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}(\rho_{\lambda}),\{\mathsf{C}_i(m_{i,\lambda})\}_{i\notin I}\rangle(1^{\lambda},1^n))$  except that whenever a Reject occurs, the distribution output is  $\bot$

{84}------------------------------------------------

We use  $\tau'$  to denote the input to the distinguisher D' where  $\tau'$  can either be  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\{r,nr\},\perp}$  or  $\mathsf{VIEW}'_{\{r,nr\},\perp}$ .

<span id="page-84-1"></span>**Claim D.2.** For any arbitrary non-uniform polynomial-size quantum distinguisher  $\mathsf{D}' = \{\mathsf{D}'_{\lambda}, \sigma_{\lambda}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ , there exists a negligible function  $\mu(\cdot)$ , such that for all adversaries  $\mathsf{C}^* = \{\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}, \rho_{\lambda}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  representing a subset of n committers, namely,  $\{\mathsf{C}_i\}_{i \in I}$  for some set  $I \subseteq [n]$ , the following holds for all polynomial-size sequences of inputs  $\{\{m_{i,\lambda}\}_{i \notin I}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ .

$$\big|\Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}'(\mathsf{VIEW}_{nr,\perp}',\sigma_{\lambda})=1] - \Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}'(\mathsf{Ext}_{nr,\perp},\sigma_{\lambda})=1]\big| \leq \mu(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* Conditioned on the event that Reject happens, both distributions (VIEW $_{nr,\perp}'$  and Ext $_{nr,\perp}$ ) output  $\perp$  by definition. Therefore, in such a case, these two distributions will be prefectly indistinguishable. Conditioned on the event that Reject does not happen, we can say that  $\tau'$  is explainable with overwhelming probability. This holds due to the soundness of ZK. Having said that, we now prove that D' cannot distinguish between real and simulated  $\tau'$ .

Suppose there exists an *arbitrary* non-uniform polynomial-size quantum distinguisher  $\mathsf{D}'=\{\mathsf{D}'_\lambda,\sigma_\lambda\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , a polynomial function  $\mathsf{poly}(\cdot)$ ,  $\mathsf{C}^*=\{\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda,\rho_\lambda\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  representing a subset of n committers, namely,  $\{\mathsf{C}_i\}_{i\in I}$  for some set  $I\subseteq [n]$ , s.t. the following holds for inifintely many polynomial-size sequence of input  $\{\{m_{i,\lambda}\}_{i\notin I}\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\lambda\in\mathbb{N}$ .

$$\big|\Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}'(\mathsf{VIEW}_{nr,\perp}',\sigma_{\lambda})=1|\neg\mathsf{Reject}]-\Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}'(\mathsf{Ext}_{nr,\perp},\sigma_{\lambda})=1|\neg\mathsf{Reject}]\big|\geq 1/\mathsf{poly}(\lambda).$$

We can use D' to build a compliant distinguisher D which contradicts the multi-committer extractability of eCom as per Definition 5.1. D first obtains a eCom transcript  $\tau$  (and adversary's state) as a challenge. It then interacts as an honest verifier with  $C_{\lambda}^*$  in |I| ZK argument sessions where  $C_{\lambda}^*$  proves that  $\tau$  is explainable. D then *verifies the ZK argument* and outputs 0 if the argument rejects. Otherwise, it forwards the entire transcript along with  $C_{\lambda}^*$ 's internal state and the value inside commitment to D'. If D' returns 1, D returns 1. Otherwise D returns 0.

Note that since non-explainable transcripts that are not rejected occur with negligible probability (due to soundness of ZK), the probability that D outputs 1 on receiving a non-explainable transcript is negligible. Therefore, D is a compliant distinguisher. Moreover, the following holds:

$$\Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}(\mathsf{VIEW}^{\mathsf{msg}}_{\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}}(\langle\mathsf{R},\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}(\rho_{\lambda}),\{\mathsf{C}_{i}(m_{i,\lambda})\}_{i\notin I}\rangle(1^{\lambda},1^{n})),\sigma_{\lambda})=1] = \Pr[\mathsf{D}'_{\lambda}(\mathsf{VIEW}'_{nr,\perp},\sigma_{\lambda})=1|\neg\mathsf{Reject}] \text{ and } \\ \Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}(\mathsf{Ext}(1^{\lambda},1^{n},I,\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda},\rho_{\lambda}),\sigma_{\lambda})=1] = \Pr[\mathsf{D}'_{\lambda}(\mathsf{Ext}_{nr,\perp},\sigma_{\lambda})=1|\neg\mathsf{Reject}]$$

Therefore,

$$\begin{split} & \left| \Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}(\mathsf{VIEW}^{\mathsf{msg}}_{\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}}(\langle \mathsf{R}, \mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}(\rho_{\lambda}), \{\mathsf{C}_{i}(m_{i,\lambda})\}_{i \notin I}\rangle(1^{\lambda}, 1^{n})), \sigma_{\lambda}) = 1] \right. \\ & \left. - \Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}(\mathsf{Ext}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{n}, I, \mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}, \rho_{\lambda}), \sigma_{\lambda}) = 1] \right| \geq 1/\mathsf{poly}(\lambda). \end{split}$$

which gives a contradiction.

<span id="page-84-0"></span>**Claim D.3.** For any arbitrary non-uniform polynomial-size quantum distinguisher  $\mathsf{D}' = \{\mathsf{D}'_{\lambda}, \sigma_{\lambda}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ , there exists a negligible function  $\mu(\cdot)$ , such that for all adversaries  $\mathsf{C}^* = \{\mathsf{C}^*_{\lambda}, \rho_{\lambda}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  representing a subset of n committers, namely,  $\{\mathsf{C}_i\}_{i \in I}$  for some set  $I \subseteq [n]$ , the following holds for all polynomial-size sequences of inputs  $\{\{m_{i,\lambda}\}_{i \notin I}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ .

$$\big|\Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}'(\mathsf{VIEW}_{r,\perp}',\sigma_{\lambda})=1] - \Pr[\mathsf{D}_{\lambda}'(\mathsf{Ext}_{r,\perp},\sigma_{\lambda})=1]\big| \leq \mu(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* Conditioned on the event that Reject does not happen, both distributions (VIEW $_{r,\perp}'$  and Ext $_{r,\perp}$ ) output  $\perp$  by definition. Therefore, in such a case, these two distributions will be prefectly indistinguishable. Conditioned on the event that Reject happens, the distribution produced by Ext $_r$  is identical to the distribution produced by an honest reveiver. This holds due to the construction of Ext $_r$ 

To complete our proof, we will introduce some additional notation:

{85}------------------------------------------------

- 1. Let  $Pr_{VIEW'}^{Reject}$  be the probability that a Reject happens in VIEW'
- 2. Let  $Pr_{\mathsf{Ext}_r}^{\mathsf{Reject}}$  be the probability that a Reject happens in  $\mathsf{Ext}_r$
- 3. Let  $Pr_{\mathsf{Ext}_{nr}}^{\mathsf{Reject}}$  be the probability that a Reject happens in  $\mathsf{Ext}_{nr}$

Following [BS20], we now show that  $VIEW' = Ext_{comb}$  via a sequence on hybrids. In particular, we show that:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{VIEW'} &\stackrel{(1)}{\equiv} (\mathsf{VIEW'} | \mathsf{Reject}) \mathsf{Pr}^{\mathsf{Reject}}_{\mathsf{VIEW'}} + (\mathsf{VIEW'} | \mathsf{NoReject}) (1 - \mathsf{Pr}^{\mathsf{Reject}}_{\mathsf{VIEW'}}) \\ &\stackrel{(2)}{\approx}_c (\mathsf{VIEW'} | \mathsf{Reject}) \mathsf{Pr}^{\mathsf{Reject}}_{\mathsf{Ext}_r} + (\mathsf{VIEW'} | \mathsf{NoReject}) (1 - \mathsf{Pr}^{\mathsf{Reject}}_{\mathsf{Ext}_{nr}}) \\ &\stackrel{(3)}{\approx}_c (\mathsf{VIEW'} | \mathsf{Reject}) \mathsf{Pr}^{\mathsf{Reject}}_{\mathsf{Ext}_r} + (\mathsf{Ext}_{nr} | \mathsf{NoReject}) (1 - \mathsf{Pr}^{\mathsf{Reject}}_{\mathsf{Ext}_{nr}}) \\ &\stackrel{(4)}{\approx}_c (\mathsf{Ext}_r | \mathsf{Reject}) \mathsf{Pr}^{\mathsf{Reject}}_{\mathsf{Ext}_r} + (\mathsf{Ext}_{nr} | \mathsf{NoReject}) (1 - \mathsf{Pr}^{\mathsf{Reject}}_{\mathsf{Ext}_{nr}}) \\ &\stackrel{(5)}{\approx}_s \mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}} \end{split}$$

#### where

- 1. The equality (1) follows by definition.
- 2. The indistinguishability (2) follows as Corollary of Claim D.3 and Claim D.2. Indeed,  $VIEW'_{r,\perp} \approx_c Ext_{r,\perp}$  in particular implies that the difference in probability that Reject happens in the real interaction versus the simulated interaction is negligible, and likewise for  $VIEW'_{nr,\perp} \approx_c Ext_{nr,\perp}$ .
- 3. The indistinguishability (3) follows as a corollary of Claim D.2. This can be seen by considering two cases. First, if the probability that Reject happens in the real interaction is negligible, then VIEW'|NoReject  $\approx_c \operatorname{Ext}_{nr}|\operatorname{NoReject}$  directly follows from Claim D.2, and the indistinguishability follows. Otherwise, this probability is non-negligible, meaning that VIEW'|Reject is efficiently sampleable. Thus, a reduction to D.2 can sample from the distribution VIEW'|Reject whenever it receives  $\perp$  from the challenger.
- 4. The indistinguishability (4) follows as a corollary of Claim D.3 via a similar analysis as the last step.
- 5. The indistinguishability (5) follows from the definition of Ext<sub>comb</sub>

Also, by an analysis similar to [BS20] Corollary 3.1, 3.2, we can say that the sucess probability of  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}}$  is negligibly close to 1/2 and therefore the success probability of  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}}$  is input-oblivious.

Now we can apply the Quantum rewinding lemma 3.1 to amplify the success probability from  $\approx 1/2$  to  $\approx 1$  following an analysis similar to [BS20]. Consider the quantum circuit  $\operatorname{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb},\mathsf{C}^*}$  which is the circuit implementation of  $\operatorname{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}}$  with hardwired input  $\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda$ , that is, the only input to  $\operatorname{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb},\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda}$  is the quantum state  $\rho$ . By denoting the success probability for input  $\rho$  by  $p(\rho)$  and setting  $\epsilon \coloneqq \operatorname{negl}(\lambda) + 2^{-\lambda \cdot \frac{3}{4}}, p_0 \coloneqq 1/4$ , and  $q \coloneqq 1/2$ , we can satisfy all the conditions for Quantum Rewinding Lemma 3.1.

This implies that trace distace between  $\mathsf{R}(\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb},C^*},\rho,\lambda)$  and  $\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb}}$  is bounded by a negligible function. Therefore, our final extractor  $\mathsf{Ext}'(1^\lambda,1^n,I,\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda,\rho)=\mathsf{R}(\mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{comb},\mathsf{C}^*_\lambda},\rho,\lambda)$  completes the extraction successfully with probability negligibly close to 1.
